2026-03-21T17:04:37.2337834Z ##[group]Run # Note: There is currently no way to distinguish between undefined variables and empty strings in GitHub Actions.
2026-03-21T17:04:37.2338678Z [36;1m# Note: There is currently no way to distinguish between undefined variables and empty strings in GitHub Actions.[0m
2026-03-21T17:04:37.2339325Z [36;1m# This limitation affects how we handle default values and empty inputs.[0m
2026-03-21T17:04:37.2339843Z [36;1m# For more information, see: https://github.com/actions/runner/issues/924[0m
2026-03-21T17:04:37.2340249Z [36;1m[0m
2026-03-21T17:04:37.2340607Z [36;1m# The following logic implements the configuration priority described in the README:[0m
2026-03-21T17:04:37.2341015Z [36;1m#[0m
2026-03-21T17:04:37.2341187Z [36;1m# Inputs[0m
2026-03-21T17:04:37.2341385Z [36;1m# Environment Variables[0m
2026-03-21T17:04:37.2341623Z [36;1m# Config File[0m
2026-03-21T17:04:37.2341825Z [36;1m# Defaults[0m
2026-03-21T17:04:37.2342004Z [36;1m#[0m
2026-03-21T17:04:37.2342429Z [36;1m# As noted above defaults are awkward to handle as GitHub Actions will inject those values as the input[0m
2026-03-21T17:04:37.2343082Z [36;1m# if the caller doesn't provide them, thus if the input matches the default we don't set it as we[0m
2026-03-21T17:04:37.2343721Z [36;1m# can't tell the difference.  Plus if we did set it when it was the default value then it could potentially[0m
2026-03-21T17:04:37.2344628Z [36;1m# override an external environment variable, or something in the callers configuration file, which then wouldn't[0m
2026-03-21T17:04:37.2345393Z [36;1m# match the configuration priority that is documented.[0m
2026-03-21T17:04:37.2345741Z [36;1mset_env_var_if_provided() {[0m
2026-03-21T17:04:37.2345993Z [36;1m  local var_name="$1"[0m
2026-03-21T17:04:37.2346223Z [36;1m  local input_value="$2"[0m
2026-03-21T17:04:37.2346467Z [36;1m  local default_value="$3"[0m
2026-03-21T17:04:37.2346699Z [36;1m[0m
2026-03-21T17:04:37.2346985Z [36;1m  if [ -n "$input_value" ] && [ "$input_value" != "$default_value" ]; then[0m
2026-03-21T17:04:37.2347456Z [36;1m    # If action was provided with explicit input by the caller set that[0m
2026-03-21T17:04:37.2347966Z [36;1m    # Use printf %q to safely escape special characters and prevent command injection[0m
2026-03-21T17:04:37.2348469Z [36;1m    printf 'export %s=%q\n' "$var_name" "$input_value" >> trivy_envs.txt[0m
2026-03-21T17:04:37.2348806Z [36;1m  fi[0m
2026-03-21T17:04:37.2348980Z [36;1m}[0m
2026-03-21T17:04:37.2349146Z [36;1m[0m
2026-03-21T17:04:37.2349432Z [36;1m# Set environment variables, handling those with default values[0m

2026-03-21T17:06:21.1448412Z ##[group]Run # Note: There is currently no way to distinguish between undefined variables and empty strings in GitHub Actions.
2026-03-21T17:06:21.1449259Z [36;1m# Note: There is currently no way to distinguish between undefined variables and empty strings in GitHub Actions.[0m
2026-03-21T17:06:21.1449910Z [36;1m# This limitation affects how we handle default values and empty inputs.[0m
2026-03-21T17:06:21.1450438Z [36;1m# For more information, see: https://github.com/actions/runner/issues/924[0m
2026-03-21T17:06:21.1450843Z [36;1m[0m
2026-03-21T17:06:21.1451215Z [36;1m# The following logic implements the configuration priority described in the README:[0m
2026-03-21T17:06:21.1451650Z [36;1m#[0m
2026-03-21T17:06:21.1451846Z [36;1m# Inputs[0m
2026-03-21T17:06:21.1452066Z [36;1m# Environment Variables[0m
2026-03-21T17:06:21.1452325Z [36;1m# Config File[0m
2026-03-21T17:06:21.1452544Z [36;1m# Defaults[0m
2026-03-21T17:06:21.1452745Z [36;1m#[0m
2026-03-21T17:06:21.1453149Z [36;1m# As noted above defaults are awkward to handle as GitHub Actions will inject those values as the input[0m
2026-03-21T17:06:21.1453847Z [36;1m# if the caller doesn't provide them, thus if the input matches the default we don't set it as we[0m
2026-03-21T17:06:21.1454727Z [36;1m# can't tell the difference.  Plus if we did set it when it was the default value then it could potentially[0m
2026-03-21T17:06:21.1455465Z [36;1m# override an external environment variable, or something in the callers configuration file, which then wouldn't[0m
2026-03-21T17:06:21.1456263Z [36;1m# match the configuration priority that is documented.[0m
2026-03-21T17:06:21.1456621Z [36;1mset_env_var_if_provided() {[0m
2026-03-21T17:06:21.1456891Z [36;1m  local var_name="$1"[0m
2026-03-21T17:06:21.1457267Z [36;1m  local input_value="$2"[0m
2026-03-21T17:06:21.1457527Z [36;1m  local default_value="$3"[0m
2026-03-21T17:06:21.1457774Z [36;1m[0m
2026-03-21T17:06:21.1458064Z [36;1m  if [ -n "$input_value" ] && [ "$input_value" != "$default_value" ]; then[0m
2026-03-21T17:06:21.1458545Z [36;1m    # If action was provided with explicit input by the caller set that[0m
2026-03-21T17:06:21.1459066Z [36;1m    # Use printf %q to safely escape special characters and prevent command injection[0m
2026-03-21T17:06:21.1459584Z [36;1m    printf 'export %s=%q\n' "$var_name" "$input_value" >> trivy_envs.txt[0m
2026-03-21T17:06:21.1459948Z [36;1m  fi[0m
2026-03-21T17:06:21.1460138Z [36;1m}[0m
2026-03-21T17:06:21.1460316Z [36;1m[0m
2026-03-21T17:06:21.1460605Z [36;1m# Set environment variables, handling those with default values[0m
